    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

        $('edition_42362558').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1983934375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7418883526699861638">I applaud Nikki for having the guts to enter that ice skating competition to help her crush and friend Brandon. Nikki's brave enough to enter even if she lacks the skills even if it makes her looks silly. What I like about this series is that teaches teens and readers to be audacious to reach for their dreams/goals.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_368838048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/368838048" />
    <a title="Theresa ♫" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5654260-theresa"><img alt="Theresa ♫" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470846673p2/5654260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/368838048?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa ♫" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa ♫" href="/user/show/5654260-theresa">Theresa ♫</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fellow humans in search for the girly version of Diary of a Wimpy Kid</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Theresa ♫ by: </span>
      NOBODY. I had to find out about the 4th book ALL BY MYSELF!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654260-theresa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654260-theresa?shelf=the-comedy-shelf">the-comedy-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654260-theresa?shelf=the-realistic-fiction-shelf">the-realistic-fiction-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654260-theresa?shelf=the-smiley-shelf">the-smiley-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654260-theresa?shelf=the-first-person-shelf">the-first-person-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654260-theresa?shelf=the-diary-shelf">the-diary-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368838048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17510864779977348316"><b>BEFORE THE BOOK HAS BEEN OPENED/READ/PURCHASED</b><br/><br/>Wait, wait, wait.<br/><br/>So . . . I was at the store . . . just browsing through the books that they had . . . and I stumbled across a bunch of copies of this book . . . and my first reaction was:<br/><br/><b>OH MY GOD, THERE'S <i>ANOTHER ONE</i>?!?!?!?!</b><br/><br/>NO ONE TOLD ME THIS! Absolutely no one. When I finished the first book, no one said, "Hey Theresa, there's a 4th book, you know."<br/><br/>AND WHY NOT?! I should know about this! I mean . . . I am a<br/><br/><b>HUGE, GIGANTIC, HYPERLY SQUEALING</b> fan of</span>
  <span id="freeText17510864779977348316" style="display:none"><b>BEFORE THE BOOK HAS BEEN OPENED/READ/PURCHASED</b><br /><br />Wait, wait, wait.<br /><br />So . . . I was at the store . . . just browsing through the books that they had . . . and I stumbled across a bunch of copies of this book . . . and my first reaction was:<br /><br /><b>OH MY GOD, THERE'S <i>ANOTHER ONE</i>?!?!?!?!</b><br /><br />NO ONE TOLD ME THIS! Absolutely no one. When I finished the first book, no one said, "Hey Theresa, there's a 4th book, you know."<br /><br />AND WHY NOT?! I should know about this! I mean . . . I am a<br /><br /><b>HUGE, GIGANTIC, HYPERLY SQUEALING</b> fan of Nikki Maxwell's adventures.<br /><br />So if there's a 5th book, someone better tell me!<br /><br />Then again, if I knew about the 4th book directly after I finished reading the third one, I would have waited for the 4th book in AGONY. So . . . the agony was avoided for now.<br /><br />BUT JEEZ, I seriously wish I knew about book number 4 sooner!<br /><br />So. My review for this lovely, lovely installment of Dork Diaries AWAITS! (Jeez, I can't wait to read it. I should have bought a copy, but alas . . . I have no money.)<br /><br />I need to read this book. This is definitely happening within the next month because if it doesn't . . .<br /><br /><i>I'm afraid heads might roll . . .</i><br /><br /><br />(As of July 29, 2012) <b>AFTER THE BOOK HAS BEEN CHECKED-OUT FROM THE LIBRARY AND READ</b><br /><br />Let me just say that Nikki Maxwell is<br /><br /><b>ONE. HUGE. DRAMA QUEEN.</b><br /><br />I know. I know. I'm such a hypocrite. Because . . . . I'm a drama queen TOO!!!!!! Y'know, except I say "Oh my god!" instead of "OMG!". If you met me about 3 years ago, you would have met my "OMG" self.<br /><br />If:<br /><br />1. You get bugged by the use of "OMG".<br />2. You get bugged by dramatic pessimism.<br />3. You get bugged by the voice of your average, overly dramatic teenage girl.<br /><br />THEN this book is not for you. Seriously.<br />Because I know a bunch of people that get SO ANNOYED by the use of "OMG" and "LOL" and "TTFN" and whatever other acronyms there are that they would KILL SOMEBODY.<br />And me being the very cautious and caring reviewer, I don't want anyone getting hurt because you got annoyed by the overflow of teenage girliness in this book.<br /><br />Anyway, I LOVE the teenage girliness in this book, mostly because, well, as cliche as it SEEMS and as many girls that walk this planet that go around shouting "OMG!" every fifteen seconds, there aren't many books like this.<br />I mean she's a fourteen year old girl.<br />I've read books about fifteen-eighteen year old girls who don't go "OMG". They just narrate with descriptions and loooooong words and melodramaticness.<br /><br />Nikki doesn't. There's no purple prose here--SHE JUST GETS RIGHT TO THE POINT.<br />And I LOVE IT.<br /><br /><br />Example: A hot guy walks by the main character.<br /><br />Melodramatic, Typical Paranormal-Romance Lead Girl (ew.): <i>He was so beautiful as he walked down the hallway, he seemed to glide like an angel. His muscles flexed gracefully as he walked towards the door. His skin glistened as he reached for the door knob, and he twisted it so slowly and angelically that I almost fainted.</i> (Please note that this particular lead girl was describing a shirtless guy opening a door.)<br /><br />Nikki Maxwell: <i>LIKE OMG! This totally hot, shirtless guy went to open the door and I almost FAINTED from how gorgeous he was!</i><br /><br />See how much time you save with Nikki Maxwell?<br /><br />And seriously. No teenage girl can be as melodramatic and descriptive as the paranormal-romance lead girls that I read about.<br /><br /><br />Well, this is just another opportunity for me to bash on paranormal romances. (I . . . dislike them.)<br /><br /><br />Anyway, the way Nikki words her words made me LAUGH. She made jokes along the way, and they were actually FUNNY!<br />Not the cheesy kind where there's the drum set in the background that goes "Bah-dump-pah!" and there are crickets chirping.<br /><br /><br />Oh, and yeah, the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[happy ending was pretty predictable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There's been one in every Nikki Maxwell book so far, but somehow, I sorta don't mind.<br /><br />This book was a FAST READ. Even though there are 344 pages (which would have taken me AGES to finish if this was a regular small print novel), I finished it within three days.<br />Maybe it's the pictures that take up the room, or that the words also take up a lot of room so there aren't as many sentences on each page and stuff.<br />Plus, the voice and the plot just had me STUCK on the book. I didn't want to stop reading!<br /><br /><br />You see, my dear fellow review readers, I really like voice.<br />EMOTION IN YOUR WRITING. That's what writing needs.<br /><br />I mean if the character only sat back and just . . . OBSERVED (like, only describing her surroundings and what things look like, but NOT giving out her thoughts and opinions), it's BORING to READ.<br />One of my best friends was reading The Hunchback of Notre Dame and there were TWO WHOLE CHAPTERS just to describe a cathedral.<br /><br />Descriptive Chapter Number One: "Notre Dame"<br />Descriptive Chapter Number Two: "Birds-Eye-View of Notre Dame"<br /><br />NO JOKE.<br />Of course my best friend skipped them.<br />And besides, don't all cathedrals look the same?<br /><br /><br />And of course, your average paranormal romances (ew).<br />The lead girl usually falls for a very hot guy, right? So she DESCRIBES the hot guy over and over and over and over and over. And yeah, she might give her opinions about how hot the guy is.<br />BUT IT DOESN'T GET TO THE POINT!<br />It's like, "OH. MY. GOD, can you just MOVE ON WITH THE STORY! The guy is hot. YOUR POINT IS MADE!"<br />Even with all those descriptions, I still can't imagine a guy THAT HOT.<br /><br /><br />Oh, and this story had your typical high school characters in them.<br /><br /><i>NIKKI MAXWELL</i> Your average teenage girl with that "OMG" habit, a family she can be embarrassed by, and no. She's not a super model.<br /><br /><i>CHLOE AND ZOEY</i> Lead girl's best friends. You can't go to high school without those, right?<br /><br /><i>MACKENZIE</i> The evil yet super-model girl, and enemy of the lead girl.<br /><br /><i>BRANDON</i> Yes, the one guy that the lead girl has a crush on.<br /><br /><br />It all seems really cliche, but I haven't found a lot of books with this kind of character build.<br />So the cliche idea isn't so cliche after all. VERY INTERESTING.<br /><br />Oh, and Nikki's reactions to things are also pretty cliche-yet-not-cliche. SHE FREAKED OUT ABOUT EVERYTHING.<br />She worried about people's thoughts about herself, and the worst things that might happen.<br /><br />I mean I think she's the kind of girl where if a guy said, "You look really pretty today," she'd say, "WHAT?! SO I LOOKED UGLY YESTERDAY?!"<br /><br /><br />Anyway, overall, if you're not freaked out by your average teenage girliness and you want a good laugh from a book, this book is the one you should put on your to-read list!<br /><br /><br />FOUR SPARKLY SPARKLY STARS.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17510864779977348316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1727998739856403068">I really enjoyed this book. It is my favorite one so far in the series, but there were a few things I would have changed. It had the best plot out of all of them currently published that I have read, however it was a little predictable. It was fun to read and I couldn't put it down, and I am glad I bought it. I will probably read it again and it is fun if you're looking for a quick read. I would say it is the girl-version of "Diary of a Wimpy Kid" and much more enjoyable for me and the illustrat</span>
  <span id="freeText1727998739856403068" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. It is my favorite one so far in the series, but there were a few things I would have changed. It had the best plot out of all of them currently published that I have read, however it was a little predictable. It was fun to read and I couldn't put it down, and I am glad I bought it. I will probably read it again and it is fun if you're looking for a quick read. I would say it is the girl-version of "Diary of a Wimpy Kid" and much more enjoyable for me and the illustrations are cute and funny. Overall, I really liked it!</span>

<div id="review_349438529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349438529" />
    <a title="Lai Valenzuela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5239575-lai-valenzuela"><img alt="Lai Valenzuela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320746042p2/5239575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349438529?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lai Valenzuela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lai Valenzuela" href="/user/show/5239575-lai-valenzuela">Lai Valenzuela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442411920" href="/book/show/13182787-tales-from-a-not-so-graceful-ice-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349438529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10959751125073415672">Book Description:<br/><br/>Nikki Maxwell isn't at all surprised to find out that her crush Brandon volunteers at a local animal shelter. He's such a sweet guy - of course he wants to help those adorable puppies! Then Brandon tells her that the shelter is in danger of closing, and Nikki knows she can't let that happen. Especially when she discovers a shocking secret about Brandon that makes keeping that shelter open more important than ever. So Nikki and her friends Chloe and Zoey enter an ice skating comp</span>
  <span id="freeText10959751125073415672" style="display:none">Book Description:<br /><br />Nikki Maxwell isn't at all surprised to find out that her crush Brandon volunteers at a local animal shelter. He's such a sweet guy - of course he wants to help those adorable puppies! Then Brandon tells her that the shelter is in danger of closing, and Nikki knows she can't let that happen. Especially when she discovers a shocking secret about Brandon that makes keeping that shelter open more important than ever. So Nikki and her friends Chloe and Zoey enter an ice skating competition to help raise money for the shelter, but (big surprise) Mackenzie has to stick her nose in and cause trouble so that she can be the one to swoop in and save the day. No way will Nikki let that happen: She'll just have to come up with some extra creative ideas this time!<br /><br />My Review:<br /><br />This book is truly amazing! Nikki is doing a holiday on ice show and the charity is called fuzzy friends since its in danger of closing down. Brandon volunteers there, so that's why she is helping. Mackenzie is mad that nikki, chloe, and zoey got it first, so she goes out of her way to sabotage their act. When u read this book, u'll figure out some secrets about brandon......<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10959751125073415672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13764082799201547975" style="display:none">I thought this book was funny of how girly the characters sounded. The genre of this book is fiction. I really liked how Nikki was willing to do anything for her crush, Brandon. I thought it was cute.<br /><br />Nikki and her friends were going to do make a performance for a charity to win ten thousand dollars, but they didn't know who they could sponsor. Their routine was fine, just that Nikki wasn't such a good skater and they fact that they couldn't find someone to sponsor was a bit more worse. But things took a bit of a twist when her crush, Brandon asked her to help him with some puppies at an animal shelter and obviously she said yes, so when she went with Brandon to help him out, she had such a good time. She later then found out that the owners of the shop were going to close and Brandon was upset. Nikki later then found out why he was so upset, it was because The owners were Brandon's grandparents and if the place closed they would have to move and Nikki wouldn't ever get to see Brandon ever again. So Nikki tried getting her act together to help Brandon out, but when it was close to performance her group's outfits disappeared and they went out as clowns and well ... they ended up doing their routine like clowns and they were falling. The thing is that everyone loved it and they ended up winning the ten thousand dollars for charity. Everything turned out fine for her and Brandon.<br /><br />I thought this was really funny because of Nikki's enemy, MacKenzie, how she was being really prissy and thought she was better because she was "popular". I think a lot of girls can relate to this because there's always that one chick trying to get in between you and your crush , like um no honey booboo child.<br /><br />I liked this book very much and i would rate it a 8.5 out of 10 because it was funny and a pretty decent book. I would recommend this book to anyone who wants to have a fun time reading or for fun. </span>

<div id="review_415429252" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415429252" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3904308-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463892304p2/3904308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415429252?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/3904308-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442411920" href="/book/show/13182787-tales-from-a-not-so-graceful-ice-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415429252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1828097292471056593">While the Diary of a Wimpy Kid series is by far the most popular series in my school library, Dork Diaries is also very popular. I must confess that I find Dork Diaries more enjoyable. Maybe it's because I don't find Greg very likeable, maybe because I can relate to a girl main character better. But I think that it is most likely because Nikki personifies so well the dramas of middle school. I have to laugh at how horrified she becomes at things that I no longer would even blink at, but which re</span>
  <span id="freeText1828097292471056593" style="display:none">While the Diary of a Wimpy Kid series is by far the most popular series in my school library, Dork Diaries is also very popular. I must confess that I find Dork Diaries more enjoyable. Maybe it's because I don't find Greg very likeable, maybe because I can relate to a girl main character better. But I think that it is most likely because Nikki personifies so well the dramas of middle school. I have to laugh at how horrified she becomes at things that I no longer would even blink at, but which really are so important to kids at that age. I also like Nikki and her friends because they are real with talents and weaknesses who often make poor decisions and then have to live with the consequences.<br /><br />In this particular book, Nikki and her best friends are putting together an ice skating routine to help save an animal rescue organization. But then Nikki tries ice skating and discovers that she has trouble just standing up. She decides to try to get out of the charity event and then finds out that her crush, Brandon, has a special connection to the shelter and she must do something to help. At the same time, Nikki's nemesis Mackenzie does everything she possibly can to make Nikki's life more difficult. <br /><br />With plenty of drama as well as humor, I couldn't help but cheer Nikki on as she struggles with her challenges both at home and at school. Girls especially will find much to enjoy in this series. The humorous illustrations add the perfect touch. I highly recommend this series to middle grade readers looking for something beyond Diary of a Wimpy Kid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1828097292471056593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_651092346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/651092346?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayleigh" href="/user/show/3089707-kayleigh">Kayleigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442411920" href="/book/show/13182787-tales-from-a-not-so-graceful-ice-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3089707-kayleigh?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer651092346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5024921649140396538">Up until this book, I'd thoroughly enjoyed this series and found it to be a fun, light, and easy read. As I continued to turn the pages, getting deeper into the story, I found myself being irritated by Nikki and her family. <br/><br/>In one chapter, the mother left fourteen year old Nikki and her six year old sister home alone to bake who knows how many Christmas cookies to hand out to friends and family. Therefore, Nikki not only had to babysit her troublemaker sister but manage not to burn the house dow</span>
  <span id="freeText5024921649140396538" style="display:none">Up until this book, I'd thoroughly enjoyed this series and found it to be a fun, light, and easy read. As I continued to turn the pages, getting deeper into the story, I found myself being irritated by Nikki and her family. <br /><br />In one chapter, the mother left fourteen year old Nikki and her six year old sister home alone to bake who knows how many Christmas cookies to hand out to friends and family. Therefore, Nikki not only had to babysit her troublemaker sister but manage not to burn the house down as well (the cookies burned so bad, a window had to be opened to release the smoke). I just couldn't believe it. At another point, Nikki started reading a book (Moby Dick for middle schoolers? Really?) she had a project due on, <b>the night before</b>. Which, by the way, the author never returned to this, leaving it hanging as to whether or not the teacher approved of what Nikki came up with (a video of her sister in the bath pretending to be a whale). There were just a lot of unrealistic things (i.e., ice skating for gym class) and I felt the story was all over the place. There were way too many ideas and I found myself forgetting what the point of the entire thing was.<br /><br />The plot was a cute one and I'm disappointed it wasn't executed as well as it could have been... but here's to hoping the next one will be better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5024921649140396538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434476366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16756184735404535270">Nikki's school, Westchester Country Day, is studying ice skating in gym so that students can participate in the Holiday on Ice charity show. Nikki signs up with her friends Chloe and Zoey in hopes that they can beat the awful MacKenzie. The only problem? Nikki can't skate. This is an even bigger problem when she chooses Fuzzy Friends as her charity-- and her crush Brandon has a big stake in that, because it is run by his grandparents, and if the animal shelter has to close, he might have to move</span>
  <span id="freeText16756184735404535270" style="display:none">Nikki's school, Westchester Country Day, is studying ice skating in gym so that students can participate in the Holiday on Ice charity show. Nikki signs up with her friends Chloe and Zoey in hopes that they can beat the awful MacKenzie. The only problem? Nikki can't skate. This is an even bigger problem when she chooses Fuzzy Friends as her charity-- and her crush Brandon has a big stake in that, because it is run by his grandparents, and if the animal shelter has to close, he might have to move. Nikki has other problems, like her goofy parents and annoying sister, having to read Moby Dick in school and do a project on it, and of course, figuring out whether or not Brandon really likes her. When MacKenzie sabotages Nikki's act for the ice show, will she be able to survive? Apparently, because Tales from a Not-So-Smart Miss Know-It-All came out on October 2nd.<br /><br />Strengths: This is what 6th grade girls mean when they want to read about romance, and reluctant readers zip through these because the pictures delude them into thinking that there isn't as much text. Very popular.<br /><br />Weaknesses: Strained my credulity on several counts-- ice skating for gym? Moby Dick? I also wanted to slap Nikki just a tiny bit for being shallow. At least she's not as annoying as Wimpy Kid.</span>

  <span id="freeText2410546313290329247" style="display:none">My 13 year old niece gave me this book which is #4 of a series she adores. I said to my self.. <div id="review_484775325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484775325" />
    <a title="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8844269-kyra-blog-of-a-bookaholic"><img alt="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489267124p2/8844269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/484775325?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)" href="/user/show/8844269-kyra-blog-of-a-bookaholic">Kyra (Blog of a Bookaholic)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer484775325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5901032946385481966">I have eagerly been awaiting for a chance to read the fourth instalment in the Dork Diaries series, Skating Sensation. When I saw it at the library I didn't hesitate to take it out, and once I got home I immediately began reading it and finished it in a few hours. I absolutely loved it and once again Rachel managed to write a charming, hilarious novel that I'm sure will be loved by many, including me.<br/><br/>In the latest instalment of fourteen year old Nikki Maxwell's interesting life, her and her two </span>
  <span id="freeText5901032946385481966" style="display:none">I have eagerly been awaiting for a chance to read the fourth instalment in the Dork Diaries series, Skating Sensation. When I saw it at the library I didn't hesitate to take it out, and once I got home I immediately began reading it and finished it in a few hours. I absolutely loved it and once again Rachel managed to write a charming, hilarious novel that I'm sure will be loved by many, including me.<br /><br />In the latest instalment of fourteen year old Nikki Maxwell's interesting life, her and her two best friends, Chloe and Zoe, sign up to do an ice-skating routine in the local village ice show to raise money for a local charity of their choice. The only problem, however, is that Nikki can't skate to save her life, but somehow she needs to try to win because suddenly the charity she is trying to help hits close to home, and if she and her friends win the ice-skating she'll be helping out one of her friends as well. With the stress of trying to learn to skate, completing her homework assignments, helping out a friend and not letting them down, as well as making sure that Mackenzie doesn't completely sabotage Nikki's chance of winning the ice-skating competition.<br /><br />I love these books, the characters are adorable, there is never a dull moment, you will catch yourself laughing out loud and marvelling at the stunning illustrations.<br /><br />Nikki is an excellent main character. She is feisty, funny, adorable, cares for her little sister, a dork, stays true to herself and doesn't change for anyone. What I love about Nikki is that she is just a normal fourteen year old, she crushes on a cute boy, has to deal with the school's mean girl and her lovable yet embarrassing family. It's nice that there are still books out there that have a normal protagonist, one that isn't a wizard or a Shadowhunter or the likes. You can relate to it more.<br /><br />The secondary characters were just as great. I loved Zoe and Chloe, Nikki's two best friends. They were sweet, goofy, kind and their optimistic and enthusiastic views made the book an even happier place to be. I would love to be friends with those three! I also love how I have things in common with Nikki, Zoe and Chloe. I also love drawing, reading, dancing etc.<br /><br />Brandon was exceptionally sweet. He was funny and sweet AND he volunteers at a local shelter to help out with all the animals, how adorable is that? I was also quite surprised to find out about Brandon's troubled home life, and I wasn't expecting it.<br /><br />Then there is Mackenzie, whom, as Nikki puts it, is a grizzly bear with fake hair extensions and a french manicure. That girl is horrible and I can't believe the lengths she will go to in order to make Nikki's life a misery. However, Nikki brushes it off and stands up to her, with the help of her friends at her side.<br /><br />I love everything about this book! From the cute, quirky characters to the stunning illustrations and the interesting storyline. I will recommend this to all girls, be they eight or sixteen, I think everyone will enjoy it! Can't wait for the next instalment!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5901032946385481966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1223181083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223181083" />
    <a title="Nora L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37044546-nora-l"><img alt="Nora L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450396005p2/37044546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223181083?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nora L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nora L" href="/user/show/37044546-nora-l">Nora L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223181083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4346219143290518460">In this realistic fiction book we follow Nikki, a dork as she travels throughout the social network of cliques, trends and gossip. The Ice-Skate-a-Thon is coming up, a charity event held by her school, and Nikki and her friends are getting ready. There is one problem though, Nikki doesn't know how to skate! Will she and her friends ever overcome these obstacles, or will their sponsor, Furry Friends go belly up? And finally, will Nikki and her crush Brandon be separated by classic mean girl Macke</span>
  <span id="freeText4346219143290518460" style="display:none">In this realistic fiction book we follow Nikki, a dork as she travels throughout the social network of cliques, trends and gossip. The Ice-Skate-a-Thon is coming up, a charity event held by her school, and Nikki and her friends are getting ready. There is one problem though, Nikki doesn't know how to skate! Will she and her friends ever overcome these obstacles, or will their sponsor, Furry Friends go belly up? And finally, will Nikki and her crush Brandon be separated by classic mean girl Mackenzie?<br /><br />Ah Dork Diaries, a well loved book written by Rachel Renée Russell about a teen undergoing the life of a dork, or as I like to call it, an insult to the very name of dork. Overall, this book was not a favorite of mine to say the least, but it was tolerable. Ever since the first book, the character conflict between Nikki and Mackenzie has developed into a hate hate relationship. On urban dictionary a dork is described as "Someone who has odd interests, and is often silly at times. A dork is also someone who can be themselves and not care what anyone thinks." The character Nikki, a self proclaimed dork goes against the very most important guideline set, being someone who can be themselves and not care. Nikki is an extremely socially conscious stereotype of a teen. With very materialistic views and values she is a very unlikeable character, with a tendency to act dopey around her crush being her only redeeming quality. If I liked the main character, I would probably have no problem with the book, as it has an excellent plot line. Honestly, Nikki's character almost has me rooting for Mackenzie!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4346219143290518460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412797983?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooklyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooklyn" href="/user/show/12736337-brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442411920" href="/book/show/13182787-tales-from-a-not-so-graceful-ice-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412797983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16852685208512849137"><br/><br/>	The book <i>Dork Diaries Tales from a Not- So- Graceful Ice Princess</i> by Rachel Renee Russell is about an 8th grade girl named Nikki. She is a girl that doesn’t have very many friends and is embarrassed by her dad who is an exterminator. In this book of the series Nikki is finally getting close to her crush, Brandon. The holiday on ice show is getting ready to start. It is a charity show to raise money. When the pet store Brandon volunteers at is closing down due to money issues, Nikki decides to g</span>
  <span id="freeText16852685208512849137" style="display:none"><br /><br />	The book <i>Dork Diaries Tales from a Not- So- Graceful Ice Princess</i> by Rachel Renee Russell is about an 8th grade girl named Nikki. She is a girl that doesn’t have very many friends and is embarrassed by her dad who is an exterminator. In this book of the series Nikki is finally getting close to her crush, Brandon. The holiday on ice show is getting ready to start. It is a charity show to raise money. When the pet store Brandon volunteers at is closing down due to money issues, Nikki decides to get her friends and skate for Fuzzy friends.<br /><br />	Nikki’s problem is she’s not the best skater. They are being coached by the famous Olympic gold metal figure skater, Victoria Steel. When they have 3 important practices right before the show, Nikki tries to distract Victoria so she doesn’t kick them of the team. The first practice she came with a “broken leg”. The second while they were skating Brandon asked Victoria to have a photo shoot. The third practice a flower delivery came for her when they were skating.<br /><br />	I love this book because, I think many people can relate to trying to do something but failing, like when a person goes out for a sport and then doesn’t do very well. I also like how the author made Victoria a mean person, by making her yell at the people who bring her coffee. I also enjoy how someone is always there to distract Victoria, like a flower delivery came right as Nikki and her friends took the ice.<br /><br />	<br /><br />	<br /></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EKLPATofCJMce8O3Vnf9CXxF3+ZREgUriElJJ4JFrF+xlyyhJXgBGAxNzNjfGnbvdTqLUD6P91YNkTt5pPoMpQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rSFaRS+Gs/+AOF1HhktJHCXC28XRofUQGnzPfwwhOWIMFLnlMOG6dJAOUigPJsL6LL2Pc748B22fpL0hKp6ZmA==')})
  }
//]]>

Julie’s the shy one: observer and artist, accidental fie<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12487708077051688367\" style=\"display:none\">Lydia Goldblatt and Julie Graham-Chang are best friends with one goal: to crack the code of popularity. Lydia’s the bold one: aspiring theater star, stick-fighting enthusiast, human guinea pig. Julie’s the shy one: observer and artist, accidental field hockey star, faithful recorder. In this notebook they write down their observations and carry out experiments to try to determine what makes the popular girls tick. But somehow, when Lydia and Julie try to imitate the popular girls, their efforts don’t translate into instant popularity. Lydia ends up with a bald spot, their parents won’t stop yelling, and Julie finds herself the number-one crush of Roland Asbjørnsen. Worse, they seem to be drifting farther and farther from their goal—and each other.\nAmy Ignatow’s hilarious debut novel introduces the intrepid fifth-graders Julie and Lydia, whose quest to understand popularity may not succeed in the ways they want, but will succeed in keeping readers in stitches.\n  From Bulletin of the Center for Children\'s Books:\n\nLydia and Julie, BFFs since birth, are now preparing to enter junior high, and they\'re on a mission to become popular. First, however, they have to determine exactly how popularity is achieved, so they decide to approach the matter as any good scientist would: observe those creatures already at the height of popularity and apply said observations to themselves, in the hopes of cracking into that mysterious world of junior-high stardom. The two record their observations and the often spectacularly unsuccessful outcomes of their various social experiments in a scrapbook-like journal, complete with notes passed at school, lists of projected popularity goals, and credibly goofy and kidlike drawings. The story here is fairly familiar: the girls fail miserably at their first attempts at the A-list (Lydia\'s hair falls out after a botched dye job, among other disasters) but eventually find acceptance in the upper echelon, only to learn the valuable lesson that it\'s the people you\'re most comfortable around who make the best friends. The diary format, however, adds an extra dimension of funny, and as in Jeff Kinney\'s Wimpy Kid series about Greg Heffley, it allows Julie and Lydia to come alive through their witty dialogue, their perceptive commentary, and even their characteristic handwriting. Secondary characters shine as well, particularly Julie\'s embarrassing but ultimately charming two dads, along with Lydia\'s goth-punk sister, a font of random quips and junior high wisdom. The popular kids end up being far from perfect and each has issues of her own to contend with, making the actual friendships that form among the girls all the more endearing. Those waiting for the next installment of Greg Heffley\'s adventures will be well served by this amusing experiment in sixth-grade celebrity.
